## Script-Level Results

### 1. Matching Regularization Ladder

`candidate_matching_regularization_ladder.py` built the opening boundary regularity ladder.

It audited:

```text
phi(R)
phi'(R)
phi''(R)
F_R = 4*pi*R^2*phi'(R)
```

Key results:

```text
value jump -> rejected,
value matching alone -> risky,
value+slope matching -> necessary diagnostic condition,
curvature / second derivative behavior -> explicit audit needed,
smooth compact toy profile -> diagnostic only,
derived support/matching law -> theorem target.
```

The C1 value-match profile still carries boundary flux:

\[
\phi(r)=\phi_0\left(1-\frac{r}{R}\right),
\]

\[
\phi(R)=0,
\]

but:

\[
\phi'(R)=-\frac{\phi_0}{R},
\]

\[
F_R=-4\pi R\phi_0.
\]

Status:

```text
CLOSED_DIAGNOSTIC
```

Consequence:

```text
value matching alone is not no-shell/no-flux proof.
```

---

### 2. Distributional Shell Source Audit

`candidate_distributional_shell_source_audit.py` audited cutoff profiles:

\[
\phi(r)=f(r)\Theta(R-r).
\]

The diagnostic derivative rule was:

\[
\frac{d}{dr}\left[f(r)\Theta(R-r)\right]
=
f'(r)\Theta(R-r)-f(R)\delta(R-r).
\]

Key results:

```text
nonzero f(R) creates value-jump delta-shell diagnostic,
f(R)=0 alone is not enough,
nonzero f'(R) can still carry boundary flux or shell-like radial diagnostic,
f(R)=0 and f'(R)=0 are necessary diagnostic no-shell/no-flux conditions,
value+slope matching is still not full support theorem.
```

Status:

```text
CLOSED_DIAGNOSTIC
```

Consequence:

```text
sharp support and value-only matching remain unsafe.
```

---

### 3. Compact Support Admissibility Conditions

`candidate_compact_support_admissibility_conditions.py` separated structural compact support from declared compact support.

Compact support is admissible only if:

```text
support origin is structural,
f(R)=0,
f'(R)=0 or equivalent no-flux condition,
distributional shell terms vanish,
support radius is not recovery-selected,
no hidden coefficient tuning occurs,
q_A_tail = 0,
C_ext = 0,
source no-double-counting is preserved.
```

Reduced witnesses:

\[
F_{\rm ext}=-4\pi C_{\rm ext},
\]

\[
\delta M_A=-\frac{c^2q_{A{\rm tail}}}{2G}.
\]

Rejected:

```text
support by declaration,
recovery-selected support,
coefficient-tuned support,
support creates boundary source,
repair object supplies support.
```

Status:

```text
REQUIRED / THEOREM_TARGET
```

Consequence:

```text
compact support is constrained but not derived.
```

---

### 4. Transition Layer Mass / Flux Audit

`candidate_transition_layer_mass_flux_audit.py` audited whether smooth layers can hide load.

A smooth transition layer is safe only if:

```text
C_layer = 0,
q_layer = 0,
I_layer = 0,
sigma_layer = 0,
alpha_recovery = 0,
source_load = 0,
layer origin is structural.
```

Reduced witnesses:

\[
F_{\rm layer}=-4\pi C_{\rm layer},
\]

\[
\delta M_A|_{\rm layer}=-\frac{c^2q_{\rm layer}}{2G},
\]

\[
\Phi_{\rm layer}=I_{\rm layer}.
\]

Thin-layer warning:

\[
\frac{\sigma_{\rm layer}}{\ell}.
\]

If \(\ell\rightarrow0\) while \(\sigma_{\rm layer}\) remains finite, the smooth layer behaves like a shell ledger.

Rejected:

```text
smoothness as neutrality,
finite-width shell disguise,
recovery-tuned transition,
transition layer scalar/A-tail repair,
transition layer source reroute,
repair object supplies layer.
```

Status:

```text
REQUIRED / THEOREM_TARGET
```

Consequence:

```text
smoothness is not neutrality.
```

# Group 29 Summary: B_s/F_zeta Coefficient Origin

## Purpose

This document records the current status of the \(B_s/F_\zeta\) coefficient-origin attempt.

Group 28 tested sector pairing / no-overlap geometry and found controlled underdetermination. It did not construct no-overlap sector geometry. The best surviving structure after Group 28 was:

```text
candidate sector inventory;
incidence/routing as best candidate forms;
zeta_Bs -> T_zeta as a candidate safe-trace anchor;
preferred next handoff: B_s/F_zeta coefficient origin.
```

Group 29 therefore asked whether coefficient origin could explain the safe scalar trace route and clarify residual interpretation.

Tiny goblin plaque:

```text
Find the metal before forging the key.
```

---

Group 29 is complete.

The main result is:

```text

Safe trace versus residual classification improved,

### 2. Volume / Trace Coefficient Origin

This script tested whether:

```text
zeta = ln sqrt(gamma)
```

and conformal-volume trace algebra can supply a structural coefficient-origin candidate.

Structural identities:

```text
delta ln sqrt(gamma) = 1/2 gamma^ij delta gamma_ij;

gamma_ij = exp(2 zeta / n) bar_gamma_ij,
with det bar_gamma fixed;

in three spatial dimensions:
gamma_ij = exp(2 zeta / 3) bar_gamma_ij.
```

Result:

```text
volume/trace algebra is a real structural candidate origin;

zeta has a natural spatial volume-trace interpretation;

B_s/F_zeta coefficient is not fixed by volume identity alone;

zeta_Bs -> T_zeta is supported but not proven;

source routing, divergence-safe behavior, residual control,
insertion, active O, and parent readiness remain not derived.
```

Status:

```text
PARTIALLY_CONSTRAINED
```

# Group 31 Summary: Source / Divergence Coefficient Law

## Purpose

This document records the current status of:

```text
31_source_divergence_coefficient_law
```

Group 30 sorted the minimal coefficient/sector postulate landscape but adopted no postulate. It left source no-double-counting and divergence-safe coefficient law theorem-route preferred. Group 31 therefore tested whether source/divergence constraints could derive or substantially constrain the \(B_s/F_\zeta\) coefficient law without explicit postulate adoption.

Tiny goblin plaque:

```text
Try to forge the key from flow, not declare a tooth.
```

---

## Main Result

Group 31 is complete.

The main result is:

```text
Source/divergence coefficient-law route produced partial constraints only.

It ruled out hidden ordinary source carriers.

It ruled out hidden divergence reservoirs.

It required visible, auditable, non-reservoir correction discipline.

It did not derive complete B_s/F_zeta coefficient law.

It did not derive trace normalization.

It did not derive safe trace membership.

It did not derive trace/residual incidence.

It did not derive B_s/F_zeta insertion.

No Group 30 candidate postulate is adopted.

Active O, residual control, and parent equation remain not ready.
```

This is a partial-constraint result, not a coefficient law.

# Explicit Minimal Postulate Selection Summary

## What This Document Is

This document summarizes the `32_explicit_minimal_postulate_selection/` development group.

It is a development summary. It is not a postulate adoption record, theorem proof, field equation, insertion theorem, active no-overlap construction, residual-control theorem, or parent closure.

The role of this group is to open and complete an explicit-choice audit after the source/divergence theorem route closed as a partial-constraint result.

The core result is:

```text
Group 32 identifies Package B as minimal plausible-to-audit under the current trace-anchor criteria.
```

The core boundary is:

```text
Package B is not selected, not adopted, and not recommended for adoption.
```

The group’s job was to make the choice surface visible, not to make the choice.

Tiny goblin summary:

```text
The teeth are counted. The bite is still a choice.
```

---

## Directory Scope

This group follows:

```text
31_source_divergence_coefficient_law
```

Group 31 established partial constraints only. It ruled out hidden ordinary source carriers and hidden divergence reservoirs, but it did not derive the complete \(B_s/F_\zeta\) coefficient law, trace normalization, safe trace membership, trace/residual incidence, insertion, active \(O\), residual control, or parent closure.

Group 32 therefore asks:

```text
Which minimal candidate postulates, if any, are we willing to adopt deliberately?
```

Equivalent safer wording:

```text
Which package is minimal plausible-to-audit if a later explicit adoption decision is made?
```

This group does not answer “yes, adopt it.”

It answers:

```text
Package B is the current minimal plausible-to-audit package.
Adoption remains separate.
```

---

## Script Sequence

The Group 32 sequence is:

```text
candidate_explicit_postulate_selection_problem.py
candidate_postulate_candidate_ledger.py
candidate_postulate_dependency_graph.py
candidate_postulate_package_sieve.py
candidate_postulate_package_minimality.py
candidate_group_32_status_summary.py
```

The conceptual arc is:

```text
open explicit-choice route
  -> classify candidate/inherited/high-risk/not-ready nodes
  -> map valid and forbidden dependency edges
  -> sieve package families
  -> test minimal plausible-to-audit status
  -> close as explicit-choice audit with no adoption
```

---

## Imported State From Group 31

Group 32 imports the following Group 31 results:

```text
hidden ordinary source carriers are ruled out as admissible shortcuts;
hidden divergence reservoirs are ruled out as admissible shortcuts;
coefficient-side ordinary source load may not be hidden;
correction/divergence load may not be hidden;
non-reservoir divergence explicitness is admissible discipline;

B_s/F_zeta insertion is not derived;
no Group 30 candidate postulate is adopted;
active O, residual control, and parent equation remain not ready.
```

The important interpretation is:

```text
Group 31 closed bad pockets.
It did not choose the coefficient law.
```

So Group 32 is allowed to audit explicit choices, but it is not allowed to pretend those choices were derived.

---

## Candidate Classes

Group 32 separates the candidates into four classes.

### Fresh Candidate Postulates

```text
P_trace_norm
P_safe_membership
```

`P_trace_norm` is the candidate choice that fixes how \(B_s\) reads the volume-trace scalar \(\zeta\) through a normalization rule.

`P_safe_membership` is the candidate choice that assigns \(\zeta_{B_s}\rightarrow T_\zeta\) as safe trace membership.

Current status:

```text
CANDIDATE_REMAINS
```

Boundary:

```text
not derived;
not adopted;
not selected from recovery;
not selected from repair;
not insertion.
```

### Inherited Discipline / Adoptable Only If Restated

```text
P_guardrail_visibility
P_div_explicitness
P_source_no_hidden
```

`P_guardrail_visibility` says boundary/source/current/mass/support loads must remain visible and auditable.

`P_div_explicitness` says correction/divergence terms must remain explicit, auditable, and non-reservoir.

`P_source_no_hidden` says ordinary source load may not hide in coefficient, residual, boundary, support, correction, exchange, curvature, or parent-placeholder channels.

Current status:

```text
INHERITED_DISCIPLINE / ADOPTABLE_ONLY_IF_RESTATED
```

Boundary:

```text
visibility is not neutrality;
explicitness is not divergence-safe law;
hidden-pocket exclusion is not full source no-double-counting theorem.
```

### High-Risk Strong Candidate

```text
P_incidence_zero
```

This would assert:

```text
I(T_zeta, R_zeta) = 0
I(T_zeta, R_kappa) = 0
```

Current status:

```text

Active \(O\), residual kill, \(B_s/F_\zeta\) insertion, and parent closure remain not ready. Any future adoption requires a separate explicit user/theory decision.

# Trace Normalization Candidate Origin Summary

## What This Document Is

This document summarizes the `33_trace_normalization_candidate_origin/` development group.

It is a group summary, not a proof archive, not a postulate adoption record, not a coefficient law, not \(B_s/F_\zeta\) insertion, and not a parent field equation.

The role of this group is to investigate whether the trace-normalization candidate identified by Group 32 can be given a structural origin or at least narrowed into visible candidate forms.

The core result is:

```text
Group 33 made the trace-normalization candidate forms visible and rejected bad selectors.
It did not select, derive, or adopt a final trace-normalization rule.
```

The safest short interpretation is:

```text
Scale-factor and metric-coefficient volume-log forms survive as compatible-if-declared candidates.
No normalization is chosen.
```

Tiny goblin summary:

```text
The cups are on the table.
No one has drunk from one.
```

---

## Directory Scope

This group contains the trace-normalization candidate-origin route following Group 32’s explicit-choice audit.

The main scripts are:

```text

```

These scripts should be read as one audit sequence:

```text

make candidate forms visible;

close the group without adoption.
```

## Locked-Door Question

The answer is:

```text
It can be structurally constrained into visible candidate forms.
It cannot yet be uniquely selected or derived.

```

---

## Structural Trace Origin

The volume-trace ledger considered \(\zeta\) as a logarithmic spatial volume trace over a traced sector of dimension \(d\).

If \(\zeta\) is total volume-log trace, then the uniform scale-factor convention gives:

\[
q = \frac{\zeta}{d}.
\]

If \(B_s\) is treated as a spatial scale factor, the candidate form is:

\[
\log(B_s)=\frac{\zeta}{d}.
\]

If \(B_s\) is treated as a spatial metric coefficient response, the candidate form is:

\[
\log(B_s)=\frac{2\zeta}{d}.
\]

The factor of two is not a recovery tune. It is the ordinary distinction between a scale factor and a metric coefficient.

Current status:

```text
STRUCTURAL_CONSTRAINT / CONVENTION_DEPENDENT
```

Current limit:

```text
This does not decide what B_s denotes.
It does not select N_trace.
```

---

## Rejected Selectors

Group 33 explicitly rejects the following ways of choosing trace normalization:

```text
recovery selector:
  AB=1, B=1/A, Schwarzschild, weak-field, gamma/PPN, or kappa=0 success;

repair selector:
  source, divergence, boundary, residual, coefficient, or matching repair;

hidden-source selector:
  hiding, cancelling, or rerouting ordinary source load;

insertion selector:
  choosing the form because it makes B_s/F_zeta insertion work;

active-O selector:
  choosing the form because it makes no-overlap O easier;

parent-fit selector:
  choosing the form because it helps close the parent equation;

membership selector:
  choosing the form because it makes zeta_Bs -> T_zeta easy;

divergence-safety selector:
  choosing the form because it appears to make divergence safety easier.
```

Current status:

```text
REJECTED_AS_SELECTOR
```

Meaning:

```text
These may sometimes audit or reject candidate forms, but they cannot choose N_trace.
```

---

## Visible Candidate Forms

Group 33 leaves five visible candidate-form families.

| Form | Candidate expression | Status | Required declaration |
|---|---|---|---|
| scale-factor volume-log | \(\log(B_s)=\zeta/d\) | `COMPATIBLE_IF_DECLARED` | \(B_s\) is scale-factor language; \(\zeta\) is total volume-log trace; \(d\) is declared |
| metric-coefficient volume-log | \(\log(B_s)=2\zeta/d\) | `COMPATIBLE_IF_DECLARED` | \(B_s\) is metric-coefficient language; \(\zeta\) is total volume-log trace; \(d\) is declared |
| per-dimension scale | \(\log(B_s)=\zeta_{pd}\) | `CONVENTION_DEPENDENT` | \(\zeta_{pd}=\zeta_{total}/d\); \(B_s\) is scale-factor language |
| per-dimension metric | \(\log(B_s)=2\zeta_{pd}\) | `CONVENTION_DEPENDENT` | \(\zeta_{pd}=\zeta_{total}/d\); \(B_s\) is metric-coefficient language |
| linearized trace-only | first-order \(\delta\ln\sqrt{\gamma}=\frac12\mathrm{tr}(h)\) | `LINEARIZED_ONLY` | first-order perturbative scope only |

None of these forms is selected.

None of these forms is adopted.

None of these forms licenses insertion.

## Compatibility Sieve Result

The compatibility sieve found:

```text
scale-factor and metric-coefficient volume-log forms survive if declared;
per-dimension forms survive only as notation-dependent variants;
linearized trace bookkeeping survives only as first-order consistency.
```

The following fail the sieve:

```text
undeclared B_s convention;
undeclared zeta convention;
undeclared traced dimension;
hidden source dependence;
hidden divergence reservoir;
membership collapse;
linearized exact-upgrade.
```

```

Current limit:

```text
Compatibility may reject or flag forms.
It cannot choose N_trace.
```

## Main Open Decisions

The group leaves four convention decisions open.

### 1. What does \(B_s\) denote?

Options include:

```text
scale-factor language;
metric-coefficient language;
separate functional response.
```

This decision matters because scale-factor and metric-coefficient conventions differ by a factor of two.

### 2. What does \(\zeta\) denote?

Options include:

```text
total volume-log trace;
per-dimension normalized trace.
```

This decision matters because per-dimension notation can hide the dimension factor.

### 3. What is the traced dimension \(d\)?

The traced sector must be declared before using \(\zeta/d\) or \(2\zeta/d\).

The dimension count must not be chosen from recovery.

### 4. Is the claim exact or linearized?

A first-order trace identity may be useful, but it is not an exact nonlinear coefficient law.

Safe membership remains a separate route or explicit decision.

It opens a non-recovery origin route, inventories volume-trace and determinant conventions, rejects recovery/repair/hidden-source/insertion/active-\(O\)/parent-fit selectors, and makes candidate forms visible. The main exact structural forms are \(\log(B_s)=\zeta/d\) if \(B_s\) is scale-factor language and \(\log(B_s)=2\zeta/d\) if \(B_s\) is metric-coefficient language, assuming \(\zeta\) is total volume-log trace over dimension \(d\). Per-dimension variants are notation-dependent, and linearized trace bookkeeping remains first-order only. No trace-normalization theorem is derived, no postulate is adopted, and no insertion or parent closure is licensed.

# Group 37 Summary: Trace Anchor Declaration Option Sieve

## What this group was for

Group 37 followed the Group 36 precondition inventory.

Group 36 counted the locks: declaration slots, status modes, safety gates, and handoff conditions. Group 37 did not fill those slots. Instead, it sorted the possible ways those slots might later be filled.

The group’s role was:

```text
prepare declaration options,
classify coherent packages,
reject shortcut packages,
and preserve the boundary between option, declaration, adoption, theorem, and insertion.
```

It was not a declaration record, adoption event, theorem proof, or insertion route.

## What the group established

Group 37 established that the trace-anchor declaration surface is no longer merely blank. There are now coherent option classes that a later explicit declaration record could choose from.

For trace normalization, the strongest active declaration-ready options are:

```text
scale-factor volume-log option:
  log(B_s) = zeta / d

metric-coefficient volume-log option:
  log(B_s) = 2 zeta / d
```

The per-dimension option survives as notation-dependent, and the linearized-only option survives as diagnostic-only. Ambiguous conventions and recovery-selected normalization are not declaration-ready.

For safe membership, the strongest active declaration-ready options are:

```text
typed trace-sector membership:
  zeta_Bs is assigned to T_zeta by explicit object, sector, domain, codomain, and criterion

role-pure trace-payload membership:
  zeta_Bs belongs to the trace sector with explicit exclusion of residual, source, correction/divergence, boundary/support, and downstream payloads
```

Diagnostic-only membership labels remain safe only if strictly inert. Residual-inclusive, source-inclusive, correction-inclusive, and incidence-collapsing membership options are rejected as shortcuts.

The joint package sieve found several coherent declaration-ready packages:

```text
scale-factor + typed membership
metric-coefficient + typed membership
scale-factor + role-pure membership
metric-coefficient + role-pure membership
```

It also fenced diagnostic-only, mixed-scope, incomplete, and hidden-load package classes.

## What the speculative batch showed

The speculative batch behaved as expected.

The opener framed the option-sieve route. The trace-normalization and safe-membership scripts classified component options without choosing them. The joint package script combined options without selecting a package. The failure-control script blocked drift from option to declaration, status, adoption, theorem, or insertion. The reconciliation script confirmed that the actual batch matched the expected option-sieve shape.

No extra reconciliation script was needed.

## What did not happen

Group 37 did not choose a declaration package.

It did not fill `B_s`, `zeta`, `d`, scope, membership-object, sector, domain/codomain, criterion, role-purity, or diagnostic/active values as theory state.

It did not assign a Package B component status.

It did not select, adopt, or derive trace normalization.

It did not select, adopt, or derive safe membership.

It did not recommend Package B adoption.

It did not derive `B_s/F_zeta` insertion, active `O`, residual control, or parent closure.

## Current status after Group 37

The current Package B status remains:

```text
Package B:
  minimal plausible-to-audit only

P_trace_norm:
  compatible-if-declared only

P_safe_membership:
  compatible-if-declared only
```

Group 37 adds:

```text
Several declaration-ready options exist.
```

That is a useful narrowing of the choice surface, but it is not itself a choice.

## Main guardrail

Do not shorten:

```text

```

to:

```text

selected form
adopted postulate
derived theorem
insertion-ready package
parent-ready package
```

Option readiness is weaker than declaration, adoption, theorem support, and downstream license.

# 38 Trace Anchor Explicit Declaration Record — Summary

## Group Purpose

Group 38 attempted to move from declaration-option audit toward an explicit trace-anchor declaration record.

The group asked whether one trace-anchor declaration package could be installed as the declared candidate surface for later theorem, adoption, or precondition routes.

## Actual Outcome

Group 38 did not complete an explicit declaration record.

Instead, it discovered and repaired a notation conflict.

The actual `B_s` usage collector found both metric-like and scale-like usage. Because those meanings differ by the factor-of-two relation between metric coefficient language and scale-factor language, the same overloaded `B_s` symbol could not safely carry both meanings.

The repair was to split the notation:

```text
B_s_metric:
  metric-coefficient spatial response branch
  candidate normalization: log(B_s_metric) = 2 zeta / d

b_s_scale:
  scale-factor / per-direction spatial response branch
  candidate normalization: log(b_s_scale) = zeta / d

F_zeta:
  neutral functional placeholder until an active branch is explicitly chosen
```

This split repairs the naming conflict, but it does not choose the active branch.

## Final Group Status

```text
DECLARATION_DEFERRED
```

Group 38 closes as a deferred declaration attempt, not as a completed declaration record.

## Current Trace-Anchor State After Group 38

```text
Package B:
  still minimal plausible-to-audit only
  still compatible-if-declared only

Trace normalization:
  not selected
  not declared
  not adopted
  not derived

Safe membership:
  not selected
  not declared
  not adopted
  not derived

B_s notation:
  conflict repaired by split
  active branch not chosen
```

## What Improved

Group 38 made the notation surface cleaner.

Before Group 38, `B_s` carried a dangerous ambiguity between metric-coefficient and scale-factor language. After Group 38, those meanings have distinct names. This prevents later scripts from hiding a factor-of-two convention choice inside one overloaded symbol.

The group therefore improved the audit state even though it did not complete the declaration.

## What Remains Open

The following remain open:

```text
explicit branch choice:
  metric_coefficient or scale_factor

trace-normalization declaration:
  B_s convention, zeta convention, traced dimension, scope, expression

safe-membership declaration:
  membership form, object, sector, domain/codomain, criterion, role purity, scope

joint Package B declaration:
  no joint declaration surface installed

adoption:
  still separate

theorem support:
  still separate

downstream use:
  not ready
```

## Guardrails Preserved

Group 38 preserves the key boundaries:

```text
notation split is not active declaration
active branch choice is not adoption
branch choice would not be theorem proof
F_zeta neutrality cannot hide a convention
Package B remains compatible-if-declared only
B_s/F_zeta insertion remains not ready
active O remains not ready
residual control remains not ready
parent equation remains not ready
```

## Recommended Next Work

There are four honest next routes.

```text
1. explicit branch-choice record
   Choose metric_coefficient or scale_factor as a declared candidate branch.

2. notation-quality source hierarchy
   Rank earliest or authoritative notation sources before choosing a branch.

3. neutral F_zeta deferral
   Keep F_zeta neutral while no concrete zeta/d or 2 zeta/d declaration is installed.

4. theorem/precondition work that does not require completed declaration
   Continue only if the route explicitly does not depend on an active B_s branch.
```

The most direct route is an explicit branch-choice record, but only if the theory owner is ready to make that choice as a declaration, not as a derivation or adoption.

## One-Line Summary

```text
Group 38 labeled the two jars but did not choose one.

# 39 Trace Anchor Branch Choice Readiness Audit — Summary

## Group Result

```text

not-ready routes
```

This lets later work proceed without confusing “this route needs a branch” with “a branch has been chosen.”

## What Was Clarified

```

No expression is installed.

`F_zeta` may remain a neutral response placeholder only if it has no concrete expression attached. It must not hide `zeta/d`, `2*zeta/d`, or any other branch-specific normalization.

### Blockers are not no-go theorems

The current blockers are missing explicit choice, unresolved evidence-quality hierarchy, and unaudited branch consequences. These do not reject either branch.

# 40 — Split-Safe Trace Anchor Precondition Audit Summary

Group 40 used the safe continuation path opened by Group 39. It asked what trace-anchor precondition work can proceed while `B_s_metric` and `b_s_scale` remain split, visible, and unchosen.

The group completed a split-safe precondition audit. It carried the two branch-indexed candidate objects in parallel, kept neutral `F_zeta` expression-free, and made several precondition surfaces explicit without turning them into declarations or theorems.

The key result is:

```text
B_s_metric and b_s_scale remain distinct candidate branches.
No active branch is chosen.
Neutral F_zeta remains safe only while expression-free.
Preconditions are visible, but not solved.
```

Group 40 clarified four useful surfaces.

First, branch-indexed candidate forms can be carried in parallel. The metric-coefficient branch and scale-factor branch may be kept visible as separate candidates, but they must not be collapsed back into overloaded `B_s` or into one neutral expression.

Second, neutral `F_zeta` remains allowed only as honest deferral. It must not hide either `zeta/d` or `2*zeta/d`.

Third, safe-membership work can continue at the precondition level. Object, sector, domain/codomain, criterion, role-purity, diagnostic scope, and exclusion-zone slots are visible, but active membership is not installed.

Fourth, residual/source/divergence/boundary safety gates are visible as gates. Source visibility, divergence explicitness, boundary/support visibility, and residual nonentry remain preconditions or theorem targets, not completed theorems.

Group 40 did not choose a branch, complete trace normalization, complete safe membership, install Package B, adopt a postulate, derive a theorem, insert `B_s/F_zeta`, construct active `O`, close residual control, or open the parent field equation.

The safe handoff is now one of these routes:

```text
explicit branch-choice record,
branch-indexed parallel declaration record,
neutral F_zeta deferral record,
safe-membership precondition continuation,
or residual/source safety theorem route.
```

The unsafe handoff remains unchanged:

```text
Do not go directly to insertion or parent closure.
```
